<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=center><B>INTRODUCTION</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify>International Barrier Technology Inc. is organized under the laws of British Columbia, Canada. &nbsp;In this Annual Report, the &#147;Company&#148;, &#147;Barrier&#148;, &#147;we&#148;, &#147;our&#148; and &#147;us&#148; refer to International Barrier Technology Inc. and its subsidiaries (unless the context otherwise requires). &nbsp;We refer you to the actual corporate documents for more complete information than may be contained in this Annual Report. &nbsp;Our principal corporate offices are located at 510 4th Street North, Watkins, Minnesota, USA &nbsp;55389. &nbsp;Our telephone number is 320-764-5797.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=center><B>BUSINESS OF INTERNATIONAL BARRIER TECHNOLOGY INC.</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify>International Barrier Technology Inc. develops, manufactures, and markets proprietary fire resistant building materials designed to help protect people and property from the destruction of fire. &nbsp;The Company uses a patented, non-combustible, non-toxic <I>Pyrotite</I> formulation that is used to coat wood panels and has potential application to engineered wood products, paint, plastics, and expanded polystyrene. &nbsp;Sales have been US$4.9 million and US$6.1 million during Fiscal 2008 and 2007, respectively.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=center><B>FINANCIAL AND OTHER INFORMATION</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify>In this Annual Report, unless otherwise specified, all dollar amounts are expressed in U.S. Dollars (&#147;$&#148;).</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>

<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=center><B>PART I</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New"><B><U>ITEM 1. &nbsp;BUSINESS</U></B></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New"><B><U>1.A. &nbsp;General Development of Business</U></B></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New"><U>Introduction</U></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify>International Barrier Technology Inc. and its subsidiaries are collectively hereinafter referred to as the &#147;Company&#148;.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify>Incorporated in July 1986, pursuant to agreements, the Company acquired the rights to the Pyrotite Technology for Canada in July 1986 and for the United States in March 1992. &nbsp;The Canadian rights and the US rights under the 1992 agreement were voluntarily terminated in January 1996 due to marketing conflict with a corporation which acquired the licensor&#146;s rights to the technology. &nbsp;A new agreement for the rights in the United States was signed in January 1996 and revised in March 1996. &nbsp;The Company acquired the world-wide rights to the Pyrotite technology, including: US patents; foreign patent filings; manufacturing know-how; trade secrets, and trademarks pursuant to a March 2004 agreement. &nbsp;The Company completed construction of a new manufacturing facility in Minnesota, USA in December 1995; the facility was upgraded to include substantial automation, increased capacity and product quality in April/May 2000.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify>The Company has been involved in the development and manufacturing/marketing of fire-rated building products since 1986, including current products: Pyrotite, a fire-barrier material comprised of the patented formulation reinforced with chopped fiberglass strands and applied by customers directly to wood sheathing designed to prevent ignition and inhibit the spread of flames; and Blazeguard&#174;, a composite fire-rated panel, composed of a coating of the patented formulation adhered to a layer of structural sheathing or oriented strand board (&#147;OSB&#148;).</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New">The Company&#146;s executive office is located at:</P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New">&nbsp;510 4th Street North, Watkins, Minnesota, USA &nbsp;55389</P>

<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify><B><U>1.C. &nbsp;Narrative Description of Business</U></B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify>International Barrier Technology Inc. (Barrier) manufactures and sells fire-rated building materials primarily in the United States. &nbsp;Barrier has a patented fire protective material (Pyrotite&#8482;) that is applied to building materials to greatly improve their respective fire resistant properties. Coated wood panel products are sold to builders through building product distribution companies all over the United States. &nbsp;Many of the top multifamily homebuilders in the US utilize Barrier&#146;s fire-rated structural panel Blazeguard&#174; in areas where the building code requires the use of a fire-rated building panel.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR>
<BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-right:24px; font-family:Courier New" align=center>5</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<HR style="margin-top:9.6px; margin-bottom:9.6px" noshade size=1.333>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New; page-break-before:always" align=justify><B><U>Seasonality</U></B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify>The building products industry in the United States does experience seasonality with housing starts generally depressed in winter months. &nbsp;Barrier&#146;s Blazeguard<FONT style="font-family:Symbol">&#226;</FONT> product, however, is sold in housing markets that have excellent winter business, including the state of Florida and California. &nbsp;Also, much of the modular housing, including the foam core panel market, performs a considerable amount of their required construction inside factories. Since the work is done within protected environments they tend to be less impacted by the winter season than typical building projects. &nbsp;Seasonality, therefore, is not considered to be a major impediment to Barrier&#146;s success in the US market place.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify><B><U>Dependency upon Patents/Licenses/Processes</U></B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify>Pursuant to an agreement for sale of technology dated 3/1/2004, between the Company and Pyrotite Corporation, the Company acquired the rights (previously licensed) to certain fire retardant technology and trademarks for $1,000,000. &nbsp;This purchase price included a $50,000 non-refundable deposit paid during the Fiscal 2003.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify>These rights and technology included all of the patents that deal with &#147;surface applied&#148; Pyrotite technology. The agreement further acknowledged that Pyrotite Corporation retained ownership of &#147;integral&#148; OSB technology (IPOSB) with a royalty to be paid to Barrier for: gross sales of any IPOBS products or substances manufactured in or sold into the US, by or on the behalf of, Pyrotite Corporation; or, for certain rights or license fees received by Pyrotite Corporation for use of the technology. &nbsp;Barrier utilizes patented manufacturing technology, as well as manufacturing know-how and trade secrets that have been developed and are closely protected by Barrier.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify>The manufacturing process for the Blazeguard<FONT style="font-family:Symbol">&#210;</FONT> product is protected by trade secrets and patent pending status on an improved technology. &nbsp;International Barrier Technology, Inc. and Barrier Technology Corporation are, in that regard, totally dependent upon these things for success in the business.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify>All employees are required to sign a Confidentiality Agreement that incorporates a &#147;do not compete clause&#148;. &nbsp;As these clauses pertain to Barrier&#146;s employees at the US operations, they have been drafted to conform to the strictest interpretation under Minnesota law.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New"><B><U>Employees</U></B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify>As of 8/31/2008, the Company had 18 full-time employees, one full time Executive Officer and two part-time Executive Officers. As of 6/30/2008, &nbsp;the Company had 22 full-time employees, one full-time Executive Officer and two part-time Executive Officers. &nbsp;There were 19 full-time employees &nbsp;as at June 30, 2007. &nbsp;None of the Company's employees are covered by collective bargaining agreements.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify><B><U>Dependency upon Customers</U></B></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify><U>Fiscal 2008</U></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify>During Fiscal 2008, the company&#146;s largest customer was MuleHide Products, Inc. &#147;Mulehide&#148;. &nbsp;Mulehide is a company that services the commercial roofing market including selling Blazeguard products to the commercial modular roof deck market. &nbsp;MuleHide purchased 74.4% of the 7,222,500 sq. ft. of Blazeguard shipped in Fiscal 2008. &nbsp;Blazeguard product shipped to MuleHide Products is private labeled MuleHide FR Deck Panel.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify>The largest market for Blazeguard products (after accounting for FR Deck Panel) in Fiscal 2008 remained roof deck applications in multifamily residential roof deck construction. &nbsp;Multifamily construction accounted for 21% of total shipments in 2008. &nbsp;Town home sales are made through building products distribution companies such as Stock Building Supply, Inc., BFS Building Supply, 84 Lumber, Inc., and Logan Lumber Company. &nbsp;The Florida market was the strongest town home market with 569,300 sq. ft. of sales (8% of total sales). &nbsp;Other town home markets include the Midwest, the mid-Atlantic region (Maryland south through North Carolina), and the northeastern USA (particularly New Jersey and Pennsylvania). &nbsp;The building products distribution companies mentioned have a presence in all of these areas and are Barrier&#146;s consistent customer throughout these geographies.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR>
<BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-right:24px; font-family:Courier New" align=center>6</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<HR style="margin-top:9.6px; margin-bottom:9.6px" noshade size=1.333>
<P style="margin:0px; page-break-before:always" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify><U>Fiscal 2007</U></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify>During Fiscal 2007, the company&#146;s largest customer was MuleHide Products, Inc. &nbsp;&nbsp;MuleHide purchased 61% of the 8,859,400 sq. ft. of Blazeguard shipped in Fiscal 2007.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify>The largest market for Blazeguard products in Fiscal 2007 remained roof deck applications in multifamily residential roof deck construction. &nbsp;Multifamily construction accounted for 39% of total shipments in 2007. &nbsp;Town home sales are made through building products distribution companies such as Stock Building Supply, Inc., BFS Building Supply, 84 Lumber, Inc., and Logan Lumber Company. &nbsp;The Florida market was the strongest town home market with 1,956,400 sq. ft. of sales (22% of total sales). &nbsp;Other town home markets include the Midwest, the mid-Atlantic region (Maryland south through North Carolina), and the northeastern USA (particularly New Jersey and Pennsylvania). &nbsp;The building products distribution companies mentioned have a presence in all of these areas and are Barrier&#146;s consistent customer throughout these geographies.</P>

<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify><B><U>1.G. &nbsp;Enforceability of Civil Liabilities</U></B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify>We are a British Columbia, Canada corporation. &nbsp;While our principal operational office and our manufacturing facility are located in the United States, our principal executive office and many of our assets are located outside of the United States. &nbsp;Additionally, a number of our directors and executive officers are residents of Canada. &nbsp;It might not be possible for investors in the United States to collect judgments obtained in United States courts predicated on the civil liability provisions of U.S. securities legislation. &nbsp;It could also be difficult to effect service of process in connection with any action brought in the United States upon such directors or executive officers. Execution by United States courts of any judgment obtained against us, or any of the directors, executive officers or experts identified in this prospectus or documents incorporated by reference herein, in United States courts would be limited to the ass
ets, or the assets of such persons or corporations, as the case might be, in the United States. &nbsp;The enforceability in Canada of United States judgments or liabilities in original actions in Canadian courts predicated solely upon the civil liability provisions of the federal securities laws of the United States is doubtful.</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New"><B><U>ITEM 1A. &nbsp;RISK FACTORS</U></B></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify>In addition to the other information presented in this Annual Report, the following should be considered carefully in evaluating the Company and its business. &nbsp;This Annual Report contains forward-looking statements that involve risks and uncertainties. &nbsp;The Company's actual results may differ materially from the results discussed in the forward-looking statements. Factors that might cause such a difference include those discussed below and elsewhere in this Annual Report.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New"><B><U>ITEM 1B. &nbsp;UNRESOLVED STAFF COMMENTS</U></B></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New">None.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR>
<BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-right:24px; font-family:Courier New" align=center>7</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<HR style="margin-top:9.6px; margin-bottom:9.6px" noshade size=1.333>
<P style="margin:0px; page-break-before:always" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=center><B>General Corporate Risks</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify><U>Investors may be disadvantaged because the Company is incorporated in Canada, which has different laws.</U></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify>The articles/by-laws and the laws of Canada are different from those typical in the United States. &nbsp;The typical rights of investors in Canadian companies differ modestly from those in the United States; refer to the relevant sections which are discussed in Section 9.A.5 and Section 10.B of this Annual Report. &nbsp;Such differences may cause investors legal difficulties.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify><U>U.S. investors may not be able to enforce their civil liabilities against the Company or its directors, controlling persons and officers.</U></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify>It may be difficult to bring and enforce suits against the Company. &nbsp;The Company is a corporation incorporated under the laws of the British Columbia, Canada. &nbsp;A majority of the Company's directors are resident outside the United States, and all or substantial portions of their assets are located outside of the United States. &nbsp;As a result, it may be difficult for U.S. holders of the Company&#146;s common shares to effect service of process on these persons within the United States or to realize in the United States upon judgments rendered against them. &nbsp;In addition, a shareholder should not assume that the courts of Canada (i) would enforce judgments of U.S. courts obtained in actions against the Company or such persons predicated upon the civil liability provisions of the U.S. federal securities laws or other laws of the United States, or (ii) would enforce, in original actions, liabilities against us or such persons predicated
 upon the U.S. federal securities laws or other laws of the United States.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify><U>Passive Foreign Investment Company (&#147;PFIC&#148;) designation could lead to an adverse tax situation for U.S. investors.</U></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify>U.S. investors in the Company could be subject to U.S. taxation at possibly adverse or higher rates and under a system that might be more complicated and unfamiliar to them. &nbsp;For example, a U.S investor might be subject to special tax rules with respect to any &#147;excess distribution&#148; received and any gain realized from a sale or other disposition (including a pledge) of that holder's shares. Distributions a U.S. investor receives in a taxable year that are greater than 125% of the average annual distributions received during the shorter of the three preceding taxable years or the holder's holding period for the shares will be treated as excess distributions. &nbsp;For example, under certain circumstances, a U.S. investor who is an individual might be subject to information reporting requirements and backup withholding, currently at a 28% rate, on dividends received on common shares. &nbsp;If a U.S. Holder holds shares in any year in wh
ich the Company is a PFIC, that holder might be required to file Internal Revenue Service Form 8621.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=center><B>Risks Relating to Financial Condition</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New"><U>The Company has accumulated losses since inception which raise substantial doubt about its ability to continue as a going concern. </U></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify>Since inception through June 30, 2008, the Company has incurred aggregate losses of $12,208,434. Our losses from operations and cash used in operations for years ended June 30, 2008 and June 30, 2007 were $808,350 and $491,023 and $79,654 and $76,746 respectively. There is no assurance that we will operate profitably or will generate positive cash flow in the future. In addition, our operating results in the future may be subject to significant fluctuations due to many factors not within our control, such as the unpredictability of when customers will order products, the size of customers' orders, the demand for our products, the level of competition or general economic conditions.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify>Although management believes that revenues will increase, management also expects an increase in &nbsp;operating costs. Consequently, the Company expects to incur operating losses and negative cash flow until our products gain market acceptance sufficient to generate a commercially viable and sustainable level of sales, and/or additional products are developed and commercially released and sales of such products made so that we are operating in a profitable manner.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR>
<BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-right:24px; font-family:Courier New" align=center>8</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<HR style="margin-top:9.6px; margin-bottom:9.6px" noshade size=1.333>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New; page-break-before:always" align=justify>The Auditors' Report on the June 30, 2008 consolidated financial statements includes an additional comment that states that there exists substantial doubt about the Company&#146;s ability to continue as a going concern. The financial statements do not include any adjustments as a result of this uncertainty.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify><U>The Company&#146;s history of operating losses is likely to lead to the need for additional, potentially unavailable, financings and related problems.</U></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify>The Company has a history of losses: ($808,350) and ($491,023) in Fiscal Years 2008 and 2007. &nbsp;Despite recent capital infusions, the Company may require significant additional funding to meet its long-term business objectives, unless the trend of losses is reversed. &nbsp;Capital may need to be available to help maintain and to expand marketing of the Company&#146;s products. &nbsp;The Company may not be able to obtain additional financing on reasonable terms, or at all. &nbsp;If equity financing is required, then such financings could result in significant dilution to existing shareholders. &nbsp;If the Company is unable to obtain sufficient financing, the Company might have to dramatically slow marketing efforts and/or lose control of its products. &nbsp;The Company has historically obtained the preponderance of its financing through the issuance of equity. &nbsp;There is a limit of 100,000,000 authorized common shares. &nbsp;The Company has
 no current plans to obtain financing through means other than equity financing and/or loans. &nbsp;Such losses and the resulting need for external financings could result in losses of investment value.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify><U>The Company&#146;s need for additional financing to expand production and conduct marketing efforts could lead to the Company&#146;s inability to continue generating material sales revenue.</U></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify>The Company develops, manufactures, and markets proprietary fire resistant building materials designed to help protect people and property from the destruction of fire. &nbsp;The Company believes it has sufficient funds to undertake its planned operations and exploration projects during Fiscal 2009. &nbsp;Small amounts of additional financing may be required to facilitate corporate operational growth and to expand marketing efforts on a short-term basis, however. &nbsp;Conventional bank financing has been established at a local bank up to $1,000,000 revolving line of credit. In July 2008, the terms of the revolving bank facility was modified to include a $500,000 capital loan being amortized by the bank over a 10 year period and which is secured by building, property and equipment. Additionally, the bank provided a $500,000 credit facility as an operating line of credit from which the Company has drawn $250,000.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify><U>The Company competes with other building materials companies that have similar operations, and many such competitor companies have operations and financial resources and industry experience far greater than those of the Company.</U></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify>Even if the Company maintains a successful marketing program, the Company will still be subject to competition from much larger and financially stronger competitors and such competition may materially adversely affect the Company&#146;s financial performance. &nbsp;Also, the Company&#146;s need to acquire inventory will require additional financial resources.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=center><B>Risks Relating to Management and Specific Operations</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify><U>The Company&#146;s Articles/By-Laws contain provisions indemnifying its officers and directors against all costs, charges and expenses incurred by them.</U></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify>The Company&#146;s Articles/By-Laws contain provisions that state, subject to applicable law, the Company shall indemnify every director or officer of the Company, subject to the limitations of the British Columbia Corporations Act, against all losses or liabilities that the Company&#146;s director or officer may sustain or incur in the execution of their duties. &nbsp;The Company&#146;s Articles/By-Laws further state that no director of officer shall be liable for any loss, damage or misfortune that may happen to, or be incurred by the Company in the execution of their duties if they acted honestly and in good faith with a view to the best interests of the Company. &nbsp;Such limitations on liability may reduce the likelihood of litigation against the Company&#146;s officers and directors and may discourage or deter its shareholders from suing the Company&#146;s officers and directors based upon breaches of their duties to the Company, though such
 an action, if successful, might otherwise benefit the Company and its shareholders.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR>
<BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-right:24px; font-family:Courier New" align=center>9</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<HR style="margin-top:9.6px; margin-bottom:9.6px" noshade size=1.333>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New; page-break-before:always" align=justify><U>Key management employees may fail to properly carry out their duties or may leave which could negatively impact corporate operations and/or stock pricing.</U></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify>While developing, manufacturing, and marketing proprietary fire resistant building materials designed to help protect people and property from the destruction of fire, the nature of the Company&#146;s business, its ability to develop a successful sales force, and to develop a competitive edge in the marketplace, depends, in large part, on its ability to attract and maintain qualified key management personnel. &nbsp;Competition for such personnel is intense and the Company may not be able to attract and retain such personnel. &nbsp;The Company&#146;s growth will depend on the efforts of its Directors (David Corcoran, Michael Huddy, Victor Yates and Craig Roberts) and its Senior Management (President/CEO/Director, Michael Huddy; and CFO/Director, David Corcoran; and Corporate Secretary, Lindsey Nauen). &nbsp;David Corcoran and Lindsey Nauen are work for the Company on a part-time basis while Michael Huddy works for the Company on a full-time basis. &
nbsp;&nbsp;The Company has no key-man life insurance and there are no written agreements with them.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-right:-19.2px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify><U>Operational Risks</U></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify>Barrier&#146;s business is based on the premise that building projects occasionally require fire resistive performance. &nbsp;Whether based on a requirement of a national or local building code, the possibility for lower insurance rates, or simply the desire for safety by a building owner, Barrier&#146;s health as a manufacturing company is based on a demand for resistive building products. &nbsp;Any factor that could mitigate the demand for fire resistive construction could have a negative impact on Barrier. &nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify>Barrier suffers a larger risk in the possibility that a new generation of technology that will impart fire resistance to building products may be developed. &nbsp;New technology may serve to decrease the demand for Barrier&#146;s Blazeguard product if the new technology proved to impart either better characteristics of fire performance or was found to be less expensive to produce and market than Blazeguard. &nbsp;Barrier&#146;s management team makes a concerted effort to stay abreast of new technologies as they are being developed. &nbsp;Barrier does this by staying in close contact with the industry via trade associations (e.g. The National Association of Home Builders, NAHB) and the independent research laboratories that are asked to test these new technologies and products as they are developed. &nbsp;However, there is no guarantee that the Company is able to adopt and utilize the new technology. &nbsp;New technologies require years of testing, 
not only in development but in use, before they are accepted and &#147;evaluated for use&#148; by the major building code agencies such as The International Code Council (ICC).</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify>Barrier&#146;s business is directly related to housing/building starts in the United States. &nbsp;Any factor resulting in a slowdown of economic activity, especially those that result in an increase in interest rates will have a negative impact on Barrier&#146;s business. &nbsp;Recently the economic climate in the US has been characterized by a decline in the rate of housing starts. &nbsp;While housing starts are expected to be lower in 2009 than in previous years, especially early in the fiscal year, the downward trend is expected to stop. &nbsp;Barrier is somewhat protected in minor housing market declines because growth is dependent upon increased market share in geographic areas we are currently not selling in such as Southern California and Texas. &nbsp;The potential for growth in sales due to improved market share is very high relative to the negative impact of a percentage decrease in housing starts.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify>Barrier presumes that corporate growth will be funded from positive cash flow, conventional bank loans, and from the occasional sale of equity to generate needed capital. &nbsp;The business plan, however, anticipates a few years of very rapid sales volume increases. &nbsp;Companies experiencing rapid growth depend upon solid support both in the market place and in the manufacturing facilities themselves. &nbsp;Insuring that capital is available to increase production capacity and to provide support materials and training in the market place is essential to success.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify>Barrier is relatively &#147;thin&#148; in its management and sales team. &nbsp;As a &#147;start-up&#148; company, Barrier has intentionally kept the number of middle and upper management and sales people at a minimum in an effort to conserve financial resources. &nbsp;As the company grows it will be essential to have new talent emerging to help provide leadership in the factories of production and in the market place to introduce the products to new markets: &nbsp;both in geography and in use. &nbsp;As long as the management/sales team is thin, the impact of losing a key player is very large. &nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR>
<BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-right:24px; font-family:Courier New" align=center>10</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<HR style="margin-top:9.6px; margin-bottom:9.6px" noshade size=1.333>
<P style="margin:0px; page-break-before:always" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify>Barrier relies on key relationships with industry leaders to maintain its position in the market place. &nbsp;Barrier is dependent upon suppliers to provide key elements of production at critical times at reasonable prices. &nbsp;While the majority of these materials are readily available and abundant, without quality suppliers providing reasonable terms of sales, Barrier would not be able to stay in business: there would be no operating or working goods of production to use in the manufacturing process. </P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify>Additionally, Barrier employs four independent sales representatives that are used to generate and maintain market share for their products in their respective territories. &nbsp;Barrier also has a full-time sales manager who serves as a salesman in the mid-western region and provides support for the independent sales representatives. &nbsp;Barrier continues to rely primarily on the sales force of the existing distribution network to cover the sales function, but where business has reached a threshold volume, independent representatives (non-employees, working on commission only) are being used to support this business within the area being served. &nbsp;Independent representatives lessen the impact on sales that could occur if Barrier should lose the assistance of the existing distribution network. &nbsp;While Barrier remains in a &#147;growth&#148; mode and has kept a relatively &#147;thin&#148; sales and marketing team, dependence upon the distr
ibution network will remain. &nbsp;Additional sales representatives will be added as business expands and the addition is warranted.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-right:-19.2px; font-family:Courier New" align=center><B>Risks Relating to the Company&#146;s Common Stock</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify><U>Principal stockholders, officers and directors have substantial control regarding stock ownership; this concentration could lead to conflicts of interest and difficulties in the &#147;public&#148; investors effecting corporate changes, and could adversely affect the Company&#146;s stock prices.</U></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify>The Company&#146;s Senior Management, Directors and greater-than-five-percent stockholders (and their affiliates), acting together, hold approximately 31% of the shares of the Company, on a diluted basis, and have the ability to control substantially all matters submitted to the Company&#146;s stockholders for approval (including the election and removal of directors and any merger, consolidation or sale of all or substantially all of the Company&#146;s assets) and to control the Company&#146;s management and affairs. &nbsp;Accordingly, this concentration of ownership may have the effect of delaying, deferring or preventing a change in control of the Company, impeding a merger, consolidation, takeover or other business combination involving the Company or discouraging a potential acquirer from making a tender offer or otherwise attempting to obtain control of the Company, which in turn could materially adversely affect the market price of the Compa
ny&#146;s stock.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify><U>Employee/Director/Consultant stock options could lead to greater concentration of stock ownership among insiders and could lead to dilution of stock ownership which could lead to depressed stock prices.</U></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify>Because the success of the Company is highly dependent upon its respective employees, the Company has granted to some or all of its key employees, Directors and consultants options to purchase common shares as non-cash incentives. &nbsp;To the extent that significant numbers of such options may be granted and exercised, the interests of the other stockholders of the Company may be diluted causing possible loss of investment value.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR>
<BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-right:24px; font-family:Courier New" align=center>11</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<HR style="margin-top:9.6px; margin-bottom:9.6px" noshade size=1.333>
<P style="margin:0px; page-break-before:always" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify><U>The Company has never declared or paid cash dividends on its common shares and does not anticipate doing so in the foreseeable future.</U></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify>There can be no assurance that the Company&#146;s Board of Directors will ever declare cash dividends, which action is exclusively within its discretion. &nbsp;Investors cannot expect to receive a dividend on the Company&#146;s common shares in the foreseeable future, if at all.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify><U>Low stock market prices and volume volatility for the Company&#146;s common shares create a risk that investors might not be able to effect purchases/sales at prices that accurately reflect corporate value.</U></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify>The market for the common shares of the Company on the OTC Bulletin Board in the United States may be highly volatile for reasons both related to the performance of the Company or events pertaining to the industry (i.e., price fluctuation/technological change/new competitor) as well as factors unrelated to the Company or its industry. &nbsp;The Company&#146;s common shares can be expected to be subject to volatility in both price and volume arising from market expectations. &nbsp;Stockholders of the Company may be unable to sell significant quantities of common shares in the public trading markets without a significant reduction in the price of the common shares.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify><U>Broker-Dealers may be discouraged from effecting transactions in the Company&#146;s common shares because they are subject to the penny stock rules.</U></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify>Rules 15g-1 through 15g-9 promulgated under the Securities Exchange Act of 1934, as amended, impose sales practice and disclosure requirements on NASD broker-dealers who make a market in &#147;penny stock&#148;. &nbsp;A penny stock generally includes any non-NASDAQ equity security that has a market price of less than $5.00 per share. &nbsp;The Company&#146;s shares are quoted on the OTC Bulletin Board in the United States and the TSX Venture Exchange in Canada. &nbsp;Trading on the OTCBB in the Company&#146;s common shares ranged from $0.13 (low) to $0.59 (high) during the period from 1/1/2007 to 12/31/2007, trading at $0.23 on 12/31/2007 and at $0.15 on 6/30/2008 and at $0.18 on 8/31/2008. &nbsp;The additional sales practice and disclosure requirements imposed upon broker-dealers may discourage broker-dealers from effecting transactions in the Company&#146;s shares, which could severely limit the market liquidity of the shares and impede the sale 
of the Company&#146;s shares in the secondary market.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify>Under the penny stock regulations, a broker-dealer selling penny stock to anyone other than an established customer or &#147;accredited investor&#148; (generally, an individual with net worth in excess of $1,000,000 or an annual income exceeding $200,000, or $300,000 together with his or her spouse) must make a special suitability determination for the purchaser and must receive the purchaser's written consent to the transaction prior to sale, unless the broker-dealer or the transaction is otherwise exempt.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify>In addition, the penny stock regulations require the broker-dealer to deliver, prior to any transaction involving a penny stock, a disclosure schedule prepared by the US SEC relating to the penny stock market, unless the broker-dealer or the transaction is otherwise exempt. &nbsp;A broker-dealer is also required to disclose commissions payable to the broker-dealer and the registered representative and current quotations for the securities. &nbsp;Finally, a broker-dealer is required to send monthly statements disclosing recent price information with respect to the penny stock held in a customer's account and information with respect to the limited market in penny stocks.</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR>
<BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-right:24px; font-family:Courier New" align=center>12</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<HR style="margin-top:9.6px; margin-bottom:9.6px" noshade size=1.333>
<P style="margin:0px; page-break-before:always"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify><B><U>ITEM 2. &nbsp;DESCRIPTION OF PROPERTY</U></B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify>The Company&#146;s operating and manufacturing facilities, along with executive offices, are located in leased premises at 510 Fourth Street North, Watkins, Minnesota. &nbsp;The Company entered into a 20-year &#147;capital lease&#148; beginning 6/1/1995. &nbsp;The lease allows the Company to purchase the facility for a small &#147;transfer fee&#148; once the 20-year lease is up and the industrial development bonds the City of Watkins issued to fund the project are paid in full.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify>The Company&#146;s manufacturing complex consists of two manufacturing lines housed in the main building. &nbsp;A 2,500 square-foot office is located in the front of this building. &nbsp;To the immediate east of the main drive, a storage building (40&#146; x 60&#146;) allows for short-term storage of untreated sheathing.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify>The earlier of the two production lines, our spray technology line, is housed nearest the offices and occupies approximately 22,000 sq. ft. of space. &nbsp;This line is primarily used for panels larger than 4&#146; x 8&#146; or for production not suited for the highly automated standard production line, including plywood. &nbsp;The mix for this line is produced in batches and fed through a reciprocating spray apparatus on to the panels. &nbsp;The fiberglass is supplied as roving and automatically chopped as it is applied to the panels. &nbsp;An infra-red oven supplies the energy to accelerate the cure of the coating; space is provided for the panels to be stacked. &nbsp;Specialty panels can be stacked in custom designed racks if required. The designed capacity from this line is 10MM board feet per shift.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify>The newer of the two lines, our automated line, is housed in the extension added to the main building in 2004. &nbsp;This portion of the building is 15,000 sq. feet and houses a completely separate line. &nbsp;This line runs at 20 feet per minute and is capable of producing over 20MM board feet per shift annually when running at 100% efficiency. &nbsp;We currently need to operate this line one shift only, but could quickly increase our capacity to meet market demand by adding shift(s). &nbsp;Automation efficiencies on this line cover: unstacking and restacking of panels; use of automated Pyrotite coating equipment, a computer controlled mixing area; automatic panel weight information fed back continuously to the operators; and a custom panel curing system. &nbsp;This line produces panels of much higher, consistent quality than the older line, at a much more marketable cost point.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify>Future growth plans may include plants modeled after this new line, placed strategically near markets of prime opportunity; built either by Barrier or with licensed partners.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify>Regardless of which line is used, the production process for the Pyrotite technology contains no hazardous or controlled substances that could raise environmental concerns. &nbsp;&nbsp;The majority of materials used in the production of Pyrotite are naturally occurring and are therefore accepted at local land-fills. &nbsp;&nbsp;Use and handling instructions for the Company&#146;s finished products are no more stringent than those required for handling other natural wood based building products.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR>
<BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-right:24px; font-family:Courier New" align=center>13</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<HR style="margin-top:9.6px; margin-bottom:9.6px" noshade size=1.333>
<P style="margin:0px; page-break-before:always" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify><B><U>ITEM 3. &nbsp;LEGAL PROCEEDINGS</U></B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify>International Barrier Technology Inc. (the Company) has received a preliminary liability and damage report from a New Jersey townhouse association in connection with a lawsuit the association has filed against its contractor, engineering consultant, property manager and the Company (the &#147; Defendants&#148;). &nbsp;The lawsuit involves alleged water damage in a 1997/1998 roof-replacement project that was allegedly caused by claimed Company product failure along with other alleged deficiencies. &nbsp;The Company first reported on the prospect of this litigation in December 2005. &nbsp;The townhouse association claims that as a result of defective product supplied, and negligent work performed by other named Defendants, the association has suffered damages of US$5,506,409.46. &nbsp;Repairs, to date, have been limited to certain townhouse units where water stains have appeared in ceiling areas. The damages claimed include the costs of repairs made 
subsequent to the initial installation work, attorney and consultant fees, and the estimated anticipated future costs for roof repairs on all units including those that have not previously required roof repairs nor have shown any sign of damage.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify>The Defendants, through their insurers, have engaged qualified experts to consider the report and to prepare a response to refute it. &nbsp;The townhouse association&#146;s request for mediation resulted in the scheduling of a &#147;non-binding&#148; mediation hearing held on 5/15/2007. &nbsp;Counsel for Barrier and the plaintiffs failed to negotiate a resolution during this mediation hearing. The parties continue to negotiate settlement terms but if the parties cannot agree to a settlement, the suit may go to court. &nbsp;The Company carries $1 million of product liability insurance, including the cost of attorney&#146;s fees, to protect itself against such claims and has documented that any damage occurring to date was the result of insufficient ventilation and incorrect installation. The Company anticipates that the claim will have no material financial impact on the Company.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify>The lawsuit by the townhouse association is the first involving the Company in 17 years of product distribution in the United States. &nbsp;Over that time, millions of square feet of the Company&#146;s products have been successfully installed for roofing and other applications.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify>The Company will report further on this matter as developments occur.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify>The Directors and the management of the Company know of no other material, active or pending, legal proceedings against them; nor is the Company involved as a plaintiff in any material proceeding or pending litigation.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify>The Directors and the management of the Company know of no active or pending proceedings against anyone that might materially adversely affect an interest of the Company.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>

<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=center><B>PART II</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New"><B><U>ITEM 5. &nbsp;MARKET FOR COMMON EQUITY AND RELATED STOCKHOLDER MATTERS</U></B></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify><B><U>Market Information</U></B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify>The Company's common shares began trading on the TSX Venture Exchange (formerly the Canadian Venture Exchange) in Toronto, Ontario, Canada, under its former name Barrier Technology Inc. in September 1986. &nbsp;The current stock symbol is &#147;IBH&#148;. &nbsp;The CUSIP number is #458968-10-4.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify>The Company&#146;s common shares began trading on the OTC Bulletin Board in August 2002 under the symbol IBTGF.OB.</P>

<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New"><B><U>The TSX Venture Exchange</U></B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify>The TSX Venture Exchange is a result of the acquisition by the Toronto Stock Exchange of the Canadian Venture Exchange (&#147;CDNX&#148;) from its member firms on 8/1/2001. &nbsp;The CDNX resulted from the merger between the Vancouver Stock Exchange and the Alberta Stock Exchange that took place on 11/29/1999, to form the CDNX. &nbsp;The TSX Venture Exchange currently operates as a complementary but independent exchange from its parent, the Toronto Stock Exchange.</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify>The initial roster of the CDNX was made up of venture companies previously listed on the Vancouver Stock Exchange or the Alberta Stock Exchange and later incorporated junior listings from the Montreal Stock Exchange, the Winnipeg Stock Exchange, and the CDN Over-The-Counter Market. &nbsp;The TSX Venture Exchange is a venture market as compared to the TSX Stock Exchange that is Canada&#146;s senior market and the Montreal Exchange that is Canada&#146;s market for derivatives products.</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify>The TSX Venture Exchange currently has five service centers: Calgary, Toronto, Vancouver, Winnipeg and Montreal. &nbsp;These service centers provide corporate finance, surveillance and marketing expertise. &nbsp;The corporate office for the TSX Venture Exchange is located in Calgary and the operations office is located in Vancouver.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify>The TSX Venture Exchange is a self-regulating organization owned and operated by the Toronto Stock Exchange, which in turn is owned by its member brokerage firms. &nbsp;It is governed by representatives of member firms and the public.</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify>Organizationally, the TSX Venture Exchange is comprised of seven business areas: Corporate Finance Services, Trading Services and Market Information Services, Compliance, Marketing, Technology, Corporate Affairs and Human Resources.</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify>The TSX Venture Exchange acts as a business link between TSX members, listed companies and investors. &nbsp;TSX Venture Exchange policies and procedures are designed to accommodate companies still in their formative stages and recognize those that are more established. &nbsp;Listings are predominately small and medium sized companies.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify>Investors in Canada are protected by the Canadian Investor Protection Fund (&#147;CIPF&#148;). The CIPF is a private trust fund established to protect customers in the event of the insolvency of a member of any of the following self-regulatory organizations: the TSX Venture Exchange; the Montreal Exchange; the Toronto Stock Exchange; the Toronto Futures Exchange; and the Investment Dealers Association of Canada.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify>Post-trade monitoring of market activity occurs in the market surveillance department. &nbsp;Sophisticated software analyses trade data from TRADETSX to detect possible market improprieties. &nbsp;A variety of surveillance and investigative tools allow the TSX Venture Exchange to perform electronic market monitoring and trade reviews.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify>The surveillance department is also responsible for monitoring and reviewing listed company activities and detecting breaches of the listing policies or the listing agreement. &nbsp;Market surveillance and listed company surveillance activities are closely coordinated.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR>
<BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-right:24px; font-family:Courier New" align=center>16</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<HR style="margin-top:9.6px; margin-bottom:9.6px" noshade size=1.333>
<P style="margin:0px; page-break-before:always" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify>Enforcement action taken by the surveillance department may include the following:</P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify>1) forcing companies to correct misleading or inaccurate disclosure which</P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;includes new releases or internet postings:</P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify>2) requiring the resignation of unacceptable directors and officers;</P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify>3) requiring cancellation and return shares to treasury;</P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify>4) requiring undertakings from directors and officers that they</P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;will ensure compliance with the listing agreement and listings policies in</P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the future;</P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify>5) requiring the termination of unacceptable investor relations services;</P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify>6) halting and suspending trading in the shares of companies;</P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify>7) de-listing companies that have contravened exchange by-laws, rules or</P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;policies.</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify>The market surveillance department issues TSX notices to inform the public of halts, suspensions, de-lists and other enforcement actions. &nbsp;All TSX notices can be found on the TSX website or INFOTSX. &nbsp;In the public interest, trading halts or suspensions are maintained until the surveillance department is satisfied that there is adequate disclosure of the company&#146;s affairs and a level playing field for investors.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify>In addition to market surveillance, the TSX Venture Exchange&#146;s compliance department is comprised of an investigative services team that conducts investigations into alleged violations of securities trading. &nbsp;The TSX Venture Exchange Conduct Review Committee determines whether a case for discipline exists. &nbsp;Disciplinary cases either result in a settlement reached between TSX Venture Exchange and the respondent or they proceed to a disciplinary hearing. &nbsp;The public can attend disciplinary hearings, view the exhibits filed and obtain copies of the decisions issued by the panel. &nbsp;If the hearing panel&#146;s decision is not acceptable to either TSX Venture Exchange or the respondent, an appeal process may be initiated.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify><B><U>Holders</U></B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify>The Company's common shares are issued in registered form and the following information is taken from the records of Pacific Corporate Trust Company (located in Vancouver, British Columbia, Canada), the registrar and transfer agent for the common shares.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify>On 9/26/2008, the Company&#146;s shareholders&#146; list showed 29,414,925 common shares outstanding and 140 registered shareholders with: 4,706,388 shares owned by 41 registered shareholders/depositories resident in Canada; 24,708,437 shares owned by 98 registered shareholders/depositories resident in the United States; and 100 shares owned by one shareholder in one other countries.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify>Based on this research and other research into the indirect holdings of other financial institutions, the Company believes that it has approximately 6000 beneficial owners of its common shares.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>

<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New"><B><U>Dividends</U></B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify>The Company has not declared any dividends since incorporation and does not anticipate that it will do so in the foreseeable future. &nbsp;The present policy of the Company is to retain future earnings for use in its operations and expansion of its business. &nbsp;There are no restrictions that limit the ability of the Company to pay dividends on common equity or that are likely to do so in the future.</P>
