<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New; page-break-before:always" align=justify><B><U>ITEM 7. &nbsp;MANAGEMENT&#146;S DISCUSSION AND ANALYSIS OR PLAN OF OPERATION</U></B></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="margin-top:6.667px; margin-bottom:6.667px; font-family:Courier New"><B>Critical Accounting Policies </B></P>
<P style="margin-top:6.667px; margin-bottom:6.667px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify>The SEC defines critical accounting policies as those that are, in management's view, important to the portrayal of the Company&#146;s financial condition and results of operations and require management's judgment. The discussion and analysis of the financial condition and results of operations is based on the audited consolidated financial statements, which have been prepared in accordance with U.S. generally accepted accounting principles (&quot;U.S.&nbsp;GAAP&quot;). The preparation of these financial statements requires the Company to make estimates and judgments that affect the reported amounts of assets, liabilities, revenue and expenses. Management bases its estimates on experience and on various assumptions that it believes are reasonable under the circumstances, the results of which form the basis for making judgments about the carrying values of assets and liabilities that are not readily apparent from othe
r sources. Actual results may differ from those estimates. The Company&#146;s critical accounting policies include: </P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New"><U>Revenue Recognition</U></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New">i) &nbsp;&nbsp;Building Supplies</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify>The Company recognizes revenue in accordance with Securities and Exchange Commission (&#147;SEC&#148;) Staff Accounting Bulletin 104, &#147;Revenue Recognition&#148;, which requires that: (i) persuasive evidence of an arrangement exists, (ii) delivery has occurred, (iii) the sales price is fixed and determinable, and (iv) collectibiltiy is reasonably assured. The Company recognizes revenue when the building supplies have been shipped and the customer has been invoiced. </P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify>ii) &nbsp;License Fees</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify>License fees revenue is recognized when the licensee records the sale of products from certain fire retardant technology known as IPOSB technology and collection is reasonably assured. There was no license fee revenue during the years ended June 30, 2008 and 2007.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New"><U>Impairment of Long-Lived Assets</U></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify>The Company reviews the recoverability of its long-lived assets as required by SFAS No.&nbsp;144, <I>Accounting for the Impairment or Disposal of Long-Lived Assets</I>, whenever events or changes in circumstances indicate that the carrying amount of such assets may not be recoverable. The estimated future cash flows are based upon, among other things, assumptions about future operating performance, and may differ from actual cash flows. Long-lived assets evaluated for impairment are grouped with other assets to the lowest level for which identifiable cash flows are largely independent of the cash flows of other groups of assets and liabilities. If the sum of the projected undiscounted cash flows (excluding interest) is less than the carrying value of the assets, the assets will be written down to the estimated fair value in the period in which the determination is made. The Company has determined that no impairment of long-lived assets exists as of
 June 30, 2008 or June 30, 2007. </P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New"><U>Stock-based Compensation</U></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New"><U>The Company accounts for all stock-based payments and awards under the fair value based method.</U></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify>Stock-based payments to non-employees are measured at the fair value of the consideration received, or the fair value of the equity instruments issued, or liabilities incurred, whichever is more reliably measurable. The fair value of stock-based payments to non-employees is periodically re-measured until the counterparty performance is complete, and any change therein is recognized over the vesting period of the award and in the same manner as if the Company had paid cash instead of paying with or using equity based instruments. The cost of the stock-based payments to non-employees that are fully vested and non-forfeitable as at the grant date &nbsp;is measured and recognized at that date. </P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR>
<BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-right:24px; font-family:Courier New" align=center>19</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<HR style="margin-top:9.6px; margin-bottom:9.6px" noshade size=1.333>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New; page-break-before:always" align=justify>The Company accounts for the granting of share purchase options to employees using the fair value method whereby all awards to employees will be recorded at fair value on the date of the grant. &nbsp;The fair value of all share purchase options are expensed over their vesting period with a corresponding increase to additional capital surplus. &nbsp;Upon exercise of share purchase options, the consideration paid by the option holder, together with the amount previously recognized in additional capital surplus, is recorded as an increase to share capital</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify>The Company uses the Black-Scholes option valuation model to calculate the fair value of share purchase options at the date of the grant. &nbsp;Option pricing models require the input of highly subjective assumptions, including the expected price volatility. &nbsp;Changes in these assumptions can materially affect the fair value estimate.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify><U>Recent Accounting Pronouncements</U></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify>In June 2006, the Financial Accounting Standards Board (&#147;FASB&#148;) issued FASB Interpretation No. 48, &#147;Accounting for Uncertainty in Income Taxes&#148;. &nbsp;The interpretation clarifies the accounting for uncertainty in income taxes recognized in a company&#146;s financial statements in accordance with Statement of Financial Accounting Standards No. 109, &#147;Accounting for Income Taxes&#148;. &nbsp;Specifically, the pronouncement prescribes a recognition threshold and a measurement attribute for the financial statement recognition and measurement of a tax position taken or expected to be taken in a tax return. &nbsp;The interpretation also provides guidance on the related derecognition, classification, interest and penalties, accounting for interim periods, disclosure and transition of uncertain tax position. &nbsp;The interpretation is effective for fiscal years beginning after December 15, 2006. &nbsp;Effective July 1, 2007, the C
ompany adopted the provisions of FIN 48. Based on the Company&#146;s assessment of FIN 48, as at July 1, 2007, there was no significant impact on the results of operations or financial position and required no adjustment to the opening balance sheet accounts. The Company&#146;s analysis supports the same conclusion, and there is no accrual for uncertain tax positions as of June 30, 2008. As a result, tabular reconciliation of beginning and ending balances would not be meaningful. If interest and penalties were to be assessed, we would charge interest to interest expense, and penalties to other operating expense. It is not anticipated that unrecognized tax benefits would significantly increase or decrease within 12 months of the reporting date. &nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify>In September 2006, the FASB issued SFAS No. 157, &#147;Fair Value Measurements&#148;. &nbsp;This Statement defines fair value as used in numerous accounting pronouncements, establishes a framework for measuring fair value in generally accepted accounting principles and expands disclosure related to the use of fair value measures in financial statements. &nbsp;SFAS 157 is effective for fiscal years beginning after November 15, 2007. The Company is currently evaluating the timing of adoption and the impact that adoption might have on its financial position or results of operations.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify>On February 15, 2007, the FASB issued SFAS No. 159 &#147;The Fair Value Option for Financial Assets and Financial Liabilities&#148;. &nbsp;This Statement establishes presentation and disclosure requirements designed to facilitate comparisons between companies that choose different measurement attributes for similar types of assets and liabilities. &nbsp;SFAS 159 is effective for fiscal years beginning after November 15, 2007. The Company is currently evaluating the impact that the adoption of SFAS No. 159 might have on its financial position or results of operations.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify>In December 2007, the FASB issued SFAS 141R &#147;Business Combinations&#148; which is effective for fiscal years beginning after December 15, 2008. SFAS 141R, which will replace FAS 141, is applicable to business combinations consummated after the effective date of December 15, 2008. &nbsp;The Company is currently evaluating the impact that the adoption of SFAS No. 141R might have on its financial position or results of operations.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify>In December 2007, the FASB also issued SFAS&nbsp;No.&nbsp;160, &#147;Non-controlling Interests in Consolidated Financial Statements, an amendment of ARB 51&#148;. SFAS&nbsp;No.&nbsp;160 will change the accounting and reporting for minority interests, which will be re-characterized as non-controlling interests and classified as a component of equity. SFAS&nbsp;No.&nbsp;160 requires retroactive adoption of the presentation and </P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR>
<BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-right:24px; font-family:Courier New" align=center>20</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<HR style="margin-top:9.6px; margin-bottom:9.6px" noshade size=1.333>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New; page-break-before:always" align=justify>disclosure requirements for existing minority interests. SFAS&nbsp;No.&nbsp;160 is effective for fiscal years beginning on or after December&nbsp;15, 2008 and interim periods within those fiscal years. The Company is currently evaluating the impact that the adoption of SFAS 160 might have on its financial positions or results of operations.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify>In March 2008, the FASB issued SFAS 161 &#147;Disclosures about Derivative Instruments and Hedging Activities &#150; an amendment of SFAS 133. &nbsp;This Statement requires enhanced disclosures about an entity&#146;s derivative and hedging activities and thereby improves the transparency of financial reporting. This Statement is effective for financial statements issued for fiscal years and interim periods beginning after November 15, 2008, with early application encouraged. This Statement encourages, but does not require, comparative disclosures for earlier periods at initial adoption. &nbsp;The Company is currently evaluating the impact that the adoption of SFAS 161 might have on its financial position or results of operations.</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify><B><U>MANAGEMENT&#146;S DISCUSSION AND ANALYSIS</U></B></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify><B><U>Equity Financing Timeline</U></B></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New">Fiscal 2007: &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Stock option exercise &nbsp;25,000 shares, $11,221</P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New">Fiscal 2008: &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;None</P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New">Fiscal 2009-to-date: &nbsp;None</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify><B><U>Fiscal 2008 Ended 6/30/2008</U></B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify>International Barrier Technology Inc. (Barrier) manufactures and sells fire-rated building materials primarily in the United States. &nbsp;Barrier has a patented fire protective material (Pyrotite&#8482;) that is applied to building materials to greatly improve their respective fire resistant properties. &nbsp;Coated wood panel products are sold to builders through building product distribution companies all over the United States. &nbsp;Many of the top multifamily homebuilders in the United States utilize Barrier&#146;s fire-rated structural panel Blazeguard&#174; in areas where the building code requires the use of a fire-rated building panel.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify><B>Discussion of Operations</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify>Barrier&#146;s financial statements are filed with both the SEC (USA) and SEDAR (Canada) and are disclosed in US dollars utilizing US generally accepted accounting principles. &nbsp;Barrier&#146;s filings with the SEC consist of quarterly reviewed financial statements on Form 10-Q and annual audited financial statements on Form 10-K. &nbsp;Barrier continues to file the above financial statements with SEDAR in Canada.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify><B><U>Sales</U> </B>revenue reported for the fiscal year ending June 30, 2008 was $4,877,605. &nbsp;Total sales volume, as measured by surface volume of product shipped, was 7,222,500 sq.ft. &nbsp;During the same period in the previous year, Barrier shipped 8,908,100 sq.ft. with sales revenue of $6,130,226.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify>The loss of sales volume, year to year, is attributed to the substantial decline in US residential housing starts. &nbsp;Barrier sold 1,517,300 sq. ft. to residential markets in FY2008, only 44 percent of what was shipped in the previous year; representing a decline in sales volume to this market of 1,950,600 sq.ft. &nbsp;All other markets experienced increases in sales volume.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify>Sales into the Commercial Modular Sector grew by four percent to 5,637,000 sq.ft., up from last year&#146;s total of 5,421,500 sq.ft. &nbsp;The remainder of the current fiscal sales volume, 68,200 sq.ft. was shipped into the SIPs (structural insulated panel) market. &nbsp;This was an increase of 49,400 sq.ft. over the 18,700 sq.ft. shipped into this market in 2007.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify>Barrier continues to expand the geographic base for Blazeguard sales in the US. Barrier and is actively marketing Blazeguard to the multi-family residential roof deck market in Southern California and in Texas. &nbsp;Barrier&#146;s wholesale building products distributor in California has invested in Blazeguard inventory and expects to see increased sales to builders and lumber dealers in the coming months.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR>
<BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-right:24px; font-family:Courier New" align=center>21</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<HR style="margin-top:9.6px; margin-bottom:9.6px" noshade size=1.333>
<P style="margin:0px; page-break-before:always" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify>In August 2008, Blazeguard&#174; was added to the short list of the California State Fire Marshall&#146;s Office (CSFM) approved products for high risk wildfire zones. &nbsp;Blazeguard&#174; is listed as an approved exterior sheathing for roof and wall applications; a &#147;limited ignition&#148; material; and, for use in soffit areas under eaves. &nbsp;Barrier is currently marketing this fact to local architects, building code officials, and builders in the area. &nbsp;The initial response has encouraged Barrier to believe that as the housing economy improves in California, Blazeguard&#174; sales there to residential markets could exceed any other area previously targeted.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify>Barrier believes that recent success in introducing Blazeguard into other market applications (such as commercial modular), and other emerging geographical locations for multi-family residential, have served to lower risk by spreading sales over a broader market playing field and making the business less vulnerable to cyclicality in any one region or product application. &nbsp;The broadening of the geographic markets served will help Barrier withstand periodic cyclicality in one market by focusing efforts and providing sales opportunities to others.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify>As the US building industry continues its recovery throughout Calendar 2008, and as housing starts continue their climb back to levels reflecting the underlying need for new homes, Barrier anticipates a significant recovery in the growth rate of Blazeguard residential sales volume. &nbsp;Barrier continues its press to add builders, one by one. &nbsp;During &#147;slow times&#148;, Barrier, and the existing Blazeguard distribution network, have found builders eager to learn about how Blazeguard can improve the value of their homes. &nbsp;Barrier&#146;s aggressive positioning during this time period has created future opportunity and set the stage for strong growth as the housing market improves.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify><B><U>Gross profit</U></B> for the Fiscal 2008 was $339,086 down from $829,020 in the previous year. &nbsp;There was a classification change during the current and prior year to include amortization and R&amp;D in cost of sales. &nbsp;Therefore, the reclassified gross margin, as a percentage of sales revenue was 7% year-to-date in comparison to 13.5% in the prior year.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify>For historical comparison purposes, and as previously reported, the gross margin less the non-cash items of amortization and R&amp;D was 17.8%, down from the 23.2% reported in 2007. &nbsp;Lower volumes of production contributed to the lower gross margins as fixed costs are spread over a smaller volume of product.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify><B><U>Cost of sales</U> </B>decreased to $4,538,519 from $5,301,206 in Fiscal 2007. &nbsp;Reduced production volumes have impacted the cost of sales directly. &nbsp;As mentioned previously, the cost of sales was reclassified to include amortization and R&amp;D expenses in this reporting period. &nbsp;After reclassification, the average cost per sq.ft. of production year to date was $0.63 in comparison to $0.60 in the year prior. &nbsp;For historical comparison purposes and as previously reported, in 2007 net of amortization and R&amp;D the average cost of production was $0.53 ($0.56 in 2008).</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify>R&amp;D expenses which were incurred as new market applications continue to be explored and developed were $144,181 vs. $219,319 in Fiscal 2007. &nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify>Included in cost of sales was amortization on plant and equipment. &nbsp;Amortization increased slightly from $246,847 in 2007 to $260,335 in 2008. &nbsp;The expense reflects scheduled depreciation of the new manufacturing line equipment and building expansion. &nbsp;The amortization of the worldwide Pyrotite technology (including patents, technical know-how, and trademarks) began when Barrier purchased it in 2004 and will continue at existing rates until it is fully depreciated (eight years). &nbsp;Neither of these items have an impact on the cash position of the Company.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify><B><U>Administrative expenses</U></B> was decreased from $1,378,896 in 2007 to $1,199,715 in 2008. &nbsp;The administrative costs per sq. ft. increased slightly for the reporting period, from $0.16 to $0.17. &nbsp;As volumes continue to increase, a reduction in the average cost of administrative expense per sq.ft. produced is expected. &nbsp;Barrier expects the reduction in the average cost of administration to have a significant impact on bottom line performance in future reporting periods.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR>
<BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-right:24px; font-family:Courier New" align=center>22</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<HR style="margin-top:9.6px; margin-bottom:9.6px" noshade size=1.333>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New; page-break-before:always" align=justify>Barrier is required to report a line item entitled &#147;stock-based compensation&#148;. &nbsp;This figure is an estimate of the value of stock options awarded to management and key personnel as a portion of their total compensation package (see section: Critical Accounting Estimates below). &nbsp;The Company uses the Black-Scholes formula to calculate the fair value of the stock options. &nbsp;While this reporting is a requirement, and a true reflection of value the company is granting to key personnel, it is a &#147;non-cash&#148; item that does not affect current operating cash flows. &nbsp;Stock-based compensation for Fiscal 2008 was $47,329, in contrast to $113,681 during the previous year.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify><B>Accounting and Audit Fees</B> are substantially lower year to date ($45,331 in 2008 vs. $91,582 in 2007). &nbsp;This is attributed to moving several tasks &#147;in-house&#148; and the completion of a tax-filing project that occurred in 2007 to capture loss/carry forward amounts for future filings.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify><B>Consulting Fees </B>increased to $19,934 this year in comparison to $3,428 in 2007. &nbsp;In June 2008, Barrier enlisted the services of the George May International Consulting Group to evaluate management practices and existing accountability requirements within the operating facility in Watkins. &nbsp;As a result, the organizational structure has been modified, and an entire layer of management removed. &nbsp;Barrier anticipates that the improved communications and accountability requirements also implemented will allow this change to occur without negatively impacting management effectiveness.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify>Fiscal 2008 <B>insurance costs</B> have decreased to $125,974 in comparison to $130,873 last year. &nbsp;The difference is due to slightly lower premiums due to lower volume of sales.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify><B>Interest on Long Term Obligations </B>has increased from $52,870 to $82,109 for the reporting period. &nbsp;This increase is a result of utilizing an operating line of credit that has enabled Barrier to grow inventory levels to anticipate customer needs<FONT style="color:#007F00"> </FONT>and to provide interim funding for short term capital requirements.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify>In July 2008, the line of credit was modified to include $500,000 of capital debt which is being amortized at the bank over a 10-year period. &nbsp;This debt for capital is being secured by the building, property, and equipment in the building. &nbsp;An additional $500,000 of credit was provided by the bank as an &#147;operating&#148; line of credit, secured by inventory, receivables, and cash. &nbsp;The current amount of debt on the operating line is $250,000.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify><B>Legal fees</B> declined significantly to $64,024 for Fiscal 2008. &nbsp;For Fiscal 2007, legal fees were $109,359. &nbsp;Legal fees were expended on activities in support of Blazeguard and Pyrotite patent and trademark registration activities for New Zealand and Australia. &nbsp;Legal fees were also incurred for Barriers registration of the trade name MycoGuard&#8482; and Firepatch&#8482; Kit. &nbsp;Barrier believes protecting its technology and trademarks is an important step in positioning itself to develop strategic partners and potential technology licensees.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify><B>Sales, marketing, and investor relations</B> expenses are considerably lower at $68,909 vs. $171,753, in comparison to the prior year. &nbsp;Sales expenses are expected to grow during Fiscal 2009 with the development of Texas, Kansas City, and the southern California territories. &nbsp;Barrier will also continue to expand upon its shareholder and customer communication programs to ensure the public is informed about business development and emerging opportunities as they arise.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify><B>Other income </B>includes income not directly related to business operations. &nbsp;Other items reported herein include $21,152 in interest income vs. $33,968 in prior year and a gain of $31,127 in foreign exchange vs. $24,885 in prior year.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify><B>Net income (loss)</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify>A net loss of ($808,350) is being reported for Fiscal 2008, whereas in fiscal 2007, a net loss of ($491,023) was reported. &nbsp;Barrier will continue its efforts to cut costs wherever it can to help offset the decline in sales volume during this steep retraction in residential construction. &nbsp;Keeping a vigilant handle on costs will help keep operational losses as low as possible and enable recovery to occur sooner and at lower volumes than previously possible.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR>
<BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-right:24px; font-family:Courier New" align=center>23</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<HR style="margin-top:9.6px; margin-bottom:9.6px" noshade size=1.333>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New; page-break-before:always" align=justify>It is important to note that even with these significant reported losses, the company experienced a negative cash flow for the year ended June 30, 2008 of only ($79,654). &nbsp;It is difficult for any small-cap company to withstand long periods of financial losses; sooner or later, the money required to operate may simply run out. &nbsp;However, the Company has continued to sustain operations through some very difficult economic times without having to experience any significant curtailment in capacity or loss of market share. &nbsp;There is urgency in addressing the negative financial statement opportunity at Barrier and Barrier&#146;s management team and Board of Directors are actively addressing these issues. &nbsp;Barrier is confident that the company will remain solvent and move into profitable territory very soon.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify><B><U>New product and market development</U></B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify>Barrier continues to invest time and financial resources in an effort to accelerate long and near term growth. &nbsp;While these expenditures take away from near term profits, research and development of new products and applications as well as market development for existing products and applications are crucial to the attainment of strategic objectives and business alliances. &nbsp;Barrier intends to grow the business to levels far beyond those currently attained and new initiatives in products and markets are necessary if these long term goals are to be achieved. &nbsp;Ongoing initiatives continue to provide opportunities for sales expansion and growth.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify>Barrier, in collaboration with MuleHide Products, continues to experience success in supply both Class A and C rated roof assemblies in commercial modular roof decks for buildings destined for military use on domestic military bases. &nbsp;A &#147;new&#148; Underwriters Laboratories (UL) listing allows a FR C board to be utilized under an alternate single-ply membrane (FPEM) while achieving a Class A system rating. &nbsp;This system significantly reduces the cost of the structure and Barrier and MuleHide believe this system has a great future in commercial modular sales.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify>In support of the strength requirements for fire and strength rated walls, Barrier completed an extensive testing protocol performed by Progressive engineering, Inc. (PEI), an ICS certified independent testing, certification, and listing laboratory. &nbsp;The results demonstrate Blazeguard&#146;s ability to improve lateral load capability (shear strength for earthquake zones) and include new span and load ratings for both roof and wall applications (allowable vertical load for snow and wind load<FONT style="color:#FF0000"> </FONT>requirements).</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify>Blazeguard treatment has always been known to increase the strength of the substrate panel, now these strength improvements are certified in a way that will improve an architect&#146;s ability to reach required designed loads in a variety of applications without having to use thicker panels to improve strength.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify>Barrier has been working with a major insulative foam producer in an attempt to develop a fire rated foam product that can be used both in the finishing of basement walls as well as in &#147;built-up&#148; commercial roof decks. &nbsp;While it is still early in the R&amp;D phase, Barrier and the foam producer has developed samples and have scheduled to fire test them in October 2008.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify>Barrier improved certain elements of the old production line in the current quarter in an effort to produce structural insulated panels (SIPs) with a more consistent surface appearance. &nbsp;SIPs were a significant business for Blazeguard from 1996&#150;1999. &nbsp;Variability in the surface appearance of the coating, however, created repeatable issues and complaints when the panels were used as an exposed interior wall surface, especially in residential applications. &nbsp;The improvements completed will help to improve the consistency of Blazeguard panels used in SIPs and make them more appealing and marketable to SIPs customers.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify><B><U>Global licensing opportunities</U></B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify>Barrier continues to solicit opportunities for licensing arrangements wherever in the world that opportunity exists. &nbsp;When interested parties inquire regarding licensing, Barrier responds with an information packet and begins an assessment of appropriateness of fit with our technology. &nbsp;Barrier believes that expansion of production capacity to meet the increased demand for Blazeguard in particular geographies or in particular market applications may be best served by cooperating with a partner company in the targeted industry when a new production facility is built. &nbsp;Barrier is exploring both joint venture and licensing scenarios as plans for future growth are discussed.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR>
<BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-right:24px; font-family:Courier New" align=center>24</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<HR style="margin-top:9.6px; margin-bottom:9.6px" noshade size=1.333>
<P style="margin:0px; page-break-before:always" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify>Any licensing agreements will be designed to protect the technology, prohibit competition, and provide for royalties to be paid to Barrier on an ongoing basis.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify>Product and technology licensing scenarios are being developed within Barrier and management is confident that licensing relationships or relationships leading to licensing contracts will be in existence in the near future.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify><B><U>Financial position &amp; financings</U></B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify>Barrier ended the period with a working capital surplus of $432,882.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify>The Company generated negative operating cash flow for the fiscal year ended June 30, 2008 of ($79,654) from $76,746 for the fiscal year ended June 30, 2007. &nbsp;The net cash outflow from operating activities for the current fiscal year ended was primarily a result of a net loss of $(808,350), an increase in accounts receivable of $109,486 and reduction of finished goods in inventory and an increase in accounts payable of $217,885. &nbsp;The Company expects to fund short-term cash needs out of current operations and supplement other short-term needs with the operating line of credit that is secured by current working capital. &nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify>Investing activities resulted in a net cash outflow of $434,095 in this year compared to a net cash outflow of $463,853 in prior year. &nbsp;The Company incurred a significant amount of $420,145 in manufacturing equipment. &nbsp;The Company does not expect any additional long-term capital needs in the near future as they recently expanded the operations with a more efficient automated process that is projected to fulfill future growth needs. &nbsp;The new automation was funded largely by a private placement coupled with operating cash flows. </P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify>Financing activities resulted in a net cash inflow of $392,859 in the current year compared to a net cash inflow of $200,804 for the same period last year. The increase in cash inflow in financing activities was primarily from obtaining more debt financing and no repayment of debt.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify>There is no assurance that we will operate profitably or will generate positive cash flow in the future. In addition, our operating results in the future may be subject to significant fluctuations due to many factors not within our control, such as the unpredictability of when customers will order products, the size of customers' orders, the demand for our products, the level of competition or general economic conditions.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify>Although management believes that revenues will increase, management also expects an increase in &nbsp;operating costs. Consequently, the Company expects to incur operating losses and negative cash flow until our products gain market acceptance sufficient to generate a commercially viable and sustainable level of sales, and/or additional products are developed and commercially released and sales of such products made so that we are operating in a profitable manner.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify>The Auditors' Report on the June 30, 2008 consolidated financial statements includes an additional comment that states that there exists substantial doubt about the Company&#146;s ability to continue as a going concern. The financial statements do not include any adjustments as a result of this uncertainty.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify><B><U>Related Party Transactions</U></B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify>During the twelve months ended June 30, 2008 the Company incurred wages and management fees of $180,504 with directors of the Company and companies with common directors. &nbsp;The Company paid $177,419 wages and management fees for the same prior year ended. </P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify><U>Other Matters</U></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify>As at June 30, 2008 and 2007, the Company had not have any off-balance sheet arrangements to report.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify>International Barrier Technology Inc. (the Company) has received a preliminary liability and damage report from a New Jersey townhouse association in connection with a lawsuit the association has filed against its contractor, engineering consultant, property manager and the Company (the &#147;Defendants&#148;). &nbsp;The lawsuit involves alleged water damage in a 1997/1998 roof replacement project that was allegedly caused by claimed Company product failure along with other alleged </P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR>
<BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-right:24px; font-family:Courier New" align=center>25</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<HR style="margin-top:9.6px; margin-bottom:9.6px" noshade size=1.333>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New; page-break-before:always" align=justify>deficiencies. &nbsp;The Company first reported on the prospect of this litigation in December 2005. &nbsp;The townhouse association claims that as a result of defective product supplied, and negligent work performed by other named Defendants, the association has suffered damages of US$5,506,409.46. &nbsp;Repairs, to date, have been limited to certain townhouse units where water stains have appeared in ceiling areas. The damages claimed include the costs of repairs made subsequent to the initial installation work, attorney and consultant fees, and the estimated anticipated future costs for roof repairs on all units including those that have not previously required roof repairs nor have shown any sign of damage.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify>The Defendants, through their insurers, have engaged qualified experts to consider the report and to prepare a response to refute it. &nbsp;The townhouse association&#146;s request for mediation resulted in the scheduling of a &#147;non-binding&#148; mediation hearing held on May 15, 2007. &nbsp;Counsel for Barrier and the plaintiffs failed to negotiate a resolution during this mediation hearing. The parties continue to negotiate settlement terms but if the parties cannot agree to a settlement, the suit may go to court. &nbsp;The Company carries $1 million of product liability insurance, including the cost of attorney&#146;s fees, to protect itself against such claims and has documented that any damage occurring to date was the result of insufficient ventilation and incorrect installation. &nbsp;The Company anticipates that the claim will have no material financial impact on the Company.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify>The lawsuit by the townhouse association is the first involving the Company in 17 years of product distribution in the United States. Over that time, millions of square feet of the Company&#146;s products have been successfully installed for roofing and other applications.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Courier New" align=justify>The Company will report further on this matter as developments occur.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>

<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; font-size:11pt" align=center><B>REPORT OF INDEPENDENT REGISTERED PUBLIC ACCOUNTING FIRM </B></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; font-size:11pt">To the Directors and Stockholders, </P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; font-size:11pt">International Barrier Technology Inc.</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; font-size:11pt" align=justify>We have audited the accompanying consolidated balance sheets of International Barrier Technology Inc. as of June 30, 2008 and the related consolidated statements of operations, cash flows and stockholders&#146; equity for the year then ended. &nbsp;These financial statements are the responsibility of the Company's management. &nbsp;Our responsibility is to express an opinion on these financial statements based on our audit.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; font-size:11pt" align=justify>We conducted our audit in accordance with the standards of the Public Company Accounting Oversight Board (United States of America). Those standards require that we plan and perform an audit to obtain reasonable assurance about whether the financial statements are free of material misstatement. The Company is not required to have, nor were we engaged to perform, an audit of its internal control over financial reporting. Our audit included consideration of internal control over financial reporting as a basis for designing audit procedures that are appropriate in the circumstances, but not for the purpose of expressing an opinion on the effectiveness of the Company&#146;s internal control over financial reporting. Accordingly, we express no such opinion. &nbsp;An audit also includes examining, on a test basis, evidence supporting the amounts and disclosures in the financial statements. An audit also includes assessing the accounting principl
es used and significant estimates made by management, as well as evaluating the overall presentation of the financial statements. We believe that our audit provides a reasonable basis for our opinion.</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; font-size:11pt" align=justify>In our opinion, these consolidated financial statements referred to above present fairly, in all material respects, the financial position of International Barrier Technology Inc as of June 30, 2008 and the results of its operations and its cash flows for the year then ended, in conformity with accounting principles generally accepted in the United States of America.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-size:11pt" align=justify>The accompanying financial statements have been prepared assuming that the Company will continue as a going concern. As discussed in Note 1 to the financial statements, the Company had an accumulated deficit of $12,208,434 at June 30, 2008 and incurred a net loss of $808,350 for the year then ended. These conditions raise substantial doubt about the Company&#146;s ability to continue as a going concern. Management&#146;s plans in regard to these matters are also described in Note 1. The financial statements do not include any adjustments that might result from the outcome of this uncertainty.</P>

<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; font-size:11pt; page-break-before:always" align=center><B>INTERNATIONAL BARRIER TECHNOLOGY INC.</B></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; font-size:11pt" align=center>NOTES TO THE CONSOLIDATED FINANCIAL STATEMENTS</P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; font-size:11pt" align=center>June 30, 2008 and 2007</P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; font-size:11pt" align=center>(<U>Stated in US Dollars</U>)</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-17.333px; font-size:11pt">Note 1</P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; text-indent:72px; font-size:11pt"><U>Nature of Operations</U></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:72px; font-size:11pt">The Company develops, manufactures and markets proprietary fire resistant building materials branded as Blazeguard in the United States of America and, as well, the Company owns the exclusive U.S. and international rights to the Pyrotite fire retardant technology.</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:72px; font-size:11pt">These financial statements have been prepared in accordance with generally accepted accounting principles in the United States of America on a going concern basis, which assumes that the Company will continue to realize its assets and discharge its obligations and commitments in the normal course of operations. Realization values may be substantially different from carrying values as shown and these financial statements do not give effect to adjustments that would be necessary to the carrying values and classification of assets and liabilities should the Company be unable to continue as a going concern. &nbsp;At June 30, 2008, the Company had an accumulated deficit of $12,208,434 (2007: &nbsp;$11,400,084) since its inception and incurred a net loss of $808,350 (2007 $ 491,023) for the year and expects to incur further losses in the development of its business, all of which casts substantial doubt about the Company&#146;s ability to co
ntinue as a going concern. &nbsp;The Company&#146;s ability to continue as a going concern is dependent upon its ability to generate future profitable operations and/or to obtain the necessary financing to meet its obligations and repay its liabilities arising from normal business operations when they come due Management expects the Company&#146;s operating cash requirement over the twelve-month period ended June 30, 2009 to be approximately $6,500,000. Management has no formal plan in place to address this concern but is considering obtaining additional funds by debt financing to the extent there is a shortfall from operations. While the Company is expending its best efforts to achieve the above plans, there is no assurance that any such activity will generate funds for operations.</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:72px; font-size:11pt">The Company was incorporated under the British Columbia Company Act and is publicly traded on the TSX Venture Exchange in Canada (&#147;TSX&#148;) and the OTC Bulletin Board in the United States of America.</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:72px; font-size:11pt">During the years ended June 30, 2008 and June 30, 2007, the Company had assets in each of Canada and the United States of America and generated sales primarily in the United States of America. </P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR>
<BR></P>
<P style="line-height:14pt; margin:0px; font-family:Courier New; font-size:12pt" align=center>35</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<HR style="margin-top:9.6px; margin-bottom:9.6px" noshade size=1.333>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; font-size:11pt; page-break-before:always">International Barrier Technology Inc.</P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; font-size:11pt">Notes to the Consolidated Financial Statements</P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; font-size:11pt">June 30, 2008 and 2007</P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; font-size:11pt">(<U>Stated in US Dollars</U>) &#150; Page 2</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-17.333px; font-size:11pt">Note 2</P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; text-indent:72px; font-size:11pt"><U>Significant Accounting Policies</U></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:72px; font-size:11pt">The preparation of financial statements in accordance with United States generally accepted accounting principles requires management to make estimates and assumptions that affect the reported amounts of assets and liabilities at the date of the financial statements and the reported amounts of revenue and expenses in the reporting period. The Company regularly evaluates estimates and assumptions related to deferred income tax asset valuations, asset impairment, stock based compensation and loss contingencies. The Company bases its estimates and assumptions on current facts, historical experience and various other factors that it believes to be reasonable under the circumstances, the results of which form the basis for making judgments about the carrying values of assets and liabilities and the accrual of costs and expenses that are not readily apparent from other sources. The actual results experienced by the Company may differ materi
ally and adversely from the Company&#146;s estimates. To the extent there are material differences between the estimates and the actual results, future results of operations will be affected.</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:72px; font-size:11pt">The financial statements have, in management&#146;s opinion, been properly prepared within the framework of the significant accounting policies summarized below:</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-17.333px; text-indent:72px; font-size:11pt">a)</P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; text-indent:96px; font-size:11pt"><U>Principles of Consolidation</U></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:96px; font-size:11pt">These consolidated financial statements include the accounts of International Barrier Technology Inc. and its wholly-owned subsidiaries, Pyrotite Coatings of Canada Inc., a Canadian company and Barrier Technology Corporation, a US company. &nbsp;All inter-company transactions and balances have been eliminated.</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-17.333px; padding-left:72px; font-size:11pt">b)</P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:72px; text-indent:24px; font-size:11pt"><U>Cash and Cash Equivalents</U></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:96px; font-size:11pt">Cash and cash equivalents consist of cash and highly liquid, short-term term deposits held at Canadian banks.</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-17.333px; padding-left:72px; font-size:11pt">c)</P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:72px; text-indent:24px; font-size:11pt"><U>Inventory</U></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:96px; font-size:11pt">Inventory is valued by management at the lower of average cost and net realizable value. &nbsp;Additionally, as required by SFAS No. 151, &#147;Inventory Costs &#150; an Amendment of ARB No. 43, Chapter 4&#148;, items such as abnormal amounts of idle facility expense, freight, handling and wasted material be recognized as current period charges rather than inventory value. &nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR>
<BR></P>
<P style="line-height:14pt; margin:0px; font-family:Courier New; font-size:12pt" align=center>36</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<HR style="margin-top:9.6px; margin-bottom:9.6px" noshade size=1.333>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; font-size:11pt; page-break-before:always">International Barrier Technology Inc.</P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; font-size:11pt">Notes to the Consolidated Financial Statements</P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; font-size:11pt">June 30, 2008 and 2007</P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; font-size:11pt">(<U>Stated in US Dollars</U>) &#150; Page 3</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-17.333px; font-size:11pt">Note 2</P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; text-indent:72px; font-size:11pt"><U>Significant Accounting Policies &#150; (cont&#146;d)</U></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-17.333px; text-indent:72px; font-size:11pt">d)</P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; text-indent:96px; font-size:11pt"><U>Plant and Equipment, Trademark and Technology Rights and Amortization</U></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:96px; font-size:11pt">Plant and equipment and trademark and technology rights are recorded at cost. &nbsp;Amortization is provided using the straight line method with the following estimated useful lives:</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<TABLE style="font-size:10pt" cellspacing=0 align=center><TR><TD valign=top><P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; font-size:11pt">Manufacturing equipment</P>
</TD><TD valign=top><P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; font-size:11pt">straight line over 5 years</P>
</TD></TR>
<TR><TD valign=top><P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; font-size:11pt">Equipment and furniture</P>
</TD><TD valign=top><P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; font-size:11pt">20% - declining balance</P>
</TD></TR>
<TR><TD valign=top><P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; font-size:11pt">Computer equipment</P>
</TD><TD valign=top><P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; font-size:11pt">30% - declining balance</P>
</TD></TR>
<TR><TD valign=top><P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; font-size:11pt">Railway spur</P>
</TD><TD valign=top><P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; font-size:11pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;4% - declining balance</P>
</TD></TR>
<TR><TD valign=top><P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; font-size:11pt">Equipment under capital lease</P>
</TD><TD valign=top><P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; font-size:11pt">20% - declining balance</P>
</TD></TR>
<TR><TD valign=top><P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; font-size:11pt">Building under capital lease</P>
</TD><TD valign=top><P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; font-size:11pt">straight line over 20 years</P>
</TD></TR>
<TR><TD valign=top><P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; font-size:11pt">Trademark and technology rights &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</P>
</TD><TD valign=top><P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; font-size:11pt">straight line over 8 years</P>
</TD></TR>
</TABLE>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:96px; font-size:11pt">Leasehold Improvements are depreciated on a straight&#150;line basis over the shorter of the lease term (being five years) or economic life. </P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-17.333px; padding-left:72px; font-size:11pt">e)</P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:72px; text-indent:24px; font-size:11pt"><U>Impairment of Long-Lived Assets</U></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:96px; font-size:11pt">The Company reviews the recoverability of its long-lived assets as required by SFAS No.&nbsp;144, <I>Accounting for the Impairment or Disposal of Long-Lived Assets</I>, whenever events or changes in circumstances indicate that the carrying amount of such assets may not be recoverable. The estimated future cash flows are based upon, among other things, assumptions about future operating performance, and may differ from actual cash flows. Long-lived assets evaluated for impairment are grouped with other assets to the lowest level for which identifiable cash flows are largely independent of the cash flows of other groups of assets and liabilities. If the sum of the projected undiscounted cash flows (excluding interest) is less than the carrying value of the assets, the assets will be written down to the estimated fair value in the period in which the determination is made. The Company has determined that no impairment of long-lived asset
s exists as of June 30, 2008 or June 30, 2007. </P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-17.333px; padding-left:72px; font-size:11pt">f)</P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:72px; text-indent:24px; font-size:11pt"><U>Leases</U></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:96px; font-size:11pt">Leases are classified as capital or operating leases. &nbsp;A lease that transfers substantially all of the benefits and risks incidental to the ownership of property is classified as a capital lease. &nbsp;At the inception of a capital lease, an asset and an obligation are recorded at an amount equal to the lesser of the present value of the minimum lease payments and the property&#146;s fair value at the beginning of the lease. &nbsp;All other leases are accounted for as operating leases wherein rental payments are expensed as incurred.</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR>
<BR></P>
<P style="line-height:14pt; margin:0px; font-family:Courier New; font-size:12pt" align=center>37</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<HR style="margin-top:9.6px; margin-bottom:9.6px" noshade size=1.333>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; font-size:11pt; page-break-before:always">International Barrier Technology Inc.</P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; font-size:11pt">Notes to the Consolidated Financial Statements</P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; font-size:11pt">June 30, 2008 and 2007</P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; font-size:11pt">(<U>Stated in US Dollars</U>) &#150; Page 4</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-17.333px; font-size:11pt">Note 2</P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; text-indent:72px; font-size:11pt"><U>Significant Accounting Policies &#150; (cont&#146;d)</U></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-17.333px; text-indent:72px; font-size:11pt">g)</P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; text-indent:96px; font-size:11pt"><U>Foreign Currency Translation</U></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:96px; font-size:11pt">The functional currency for the Company&#146;s operations is the US dollar. Monetary assets and liabilities denominated in Canadian dollars are translated into U.S. dollars at the exchange rate prevailing at the end of the year. &nbsp;Non-monetary assets and liabilities are translated at the exchange rate prevailing at the respective transaction dates while revenues and expenses are translated at the average exchange rate during the year. &nbsp;Exchange gains and losses are recognized in income. </P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-17.333px; text-indent:72px; font-size:11pt">h)</P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; text-indent:96px; font-size:11pt"><U>Research and Development Costs</U></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:96px; font-size:11pt">Research and development costs are expensed in the year in which they are incurred.</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-17.333px; padding-left:72px; font-size:11pt">i)</P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:72px; text-indent:24px; font-size:11pt"><U>Basic and Diluted Loss Per Share </U></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:96px; font-size:11pt">Basic earnings per share are computed by dividing the loss for the year by the weighted average number of common shares outstanding during the year. &nbsp;Diluted earnings per share reflect the potential dilution that could occur if potentially dilutive securities were exercised or converted to common stock. &nbsp;The dilutive effect of options and warrants and their equivalent is computed by application of the treasury stock method and the effect of convertible securities by the &#147;if converted&#148; method. &nbsp;Fully dilutive amounts are not presented when the effect of the computations are anti-dilutive due to the losses incurred. &nbsp;Accordingly, there is no difference in the amounts presented for basic and diluted loss per share.</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:96px; font-size:11pt">The weighted average number of common shares outstanding for 2007 has been revised from the original calculation to correct an error in the computation. &nbsp;The impact of the change did not result in a change in the Company&#146;s loss per share for the year ended June 30, 2007.</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-17.333px; text-indent:72px; font-size:11pt">j)</P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; text-indent:96px; font-size:11pt"><U>Financial Instruments</U></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:96px; font-size:11pt">Fair Value of Financial Instruments</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:96px; font-size:11pt">The Company&#146;s financial instruments consist of cash and cash equivalents, accounts receivable, accounts payable and accrued liabilities, long-term debt and obligation under capital leases. &nbsp;Unless otherwise noted, the fair values of these financial instruments approximate their carrying values.</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR>
<BR></P>
<P style="line-height:14pt; margin:0px; font-family:Courier New; font-size:12pt" align=center>38</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<HR style="margin-top:9.6px; margin-bottom:9.6px" noshade size=1.333>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; font-size:11pt; page-break-before:always">International Barrier Technology Inc.</P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; font-size:11pt">Notes to the Consolidated Financial Statements</P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; font-size:11pt">June 30, 2008 and 2007</P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; font-size:11pt">(<U>Stated in US Dollars</U>) &#150; Page 5</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-17.333px; font-size:11pt">Note 2</P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; text-indent:72px; font-size:11pt"><U>Significant Accounting Policies</U> &#150; (cont&#146;d)</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-17.333px; padding-left:72px; font-size:11pt">k)</P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:72px; text-indent:24px; font-size:11pt">Accounts Receivable and Concentrations of Credit Risk</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:96px; font-size:11pt">The Company grants credit to its customers in the normal course of business. Trade receivables are typically non-interest bearing and are initially recorded at cost. Sales to the Company&#146;s recurring customers are generally made on open account terms Past due status of customer accounts is determined based on how recently payments have been received in relation to payment terms granted. Credit is generally extended based upon an evaluation of each customer&#146;s financial condition, with terms consistent in the industry and no collateral required. Losses from credit sales, if any, are provided for in the financial statements. &nbsp;The Company reviews its accounts receivable for collectibility based on an evaluation of specific customer risks along with historical and probable bad debt experience. Management determined that no allowance was necessary at June 30, 2008 and 2007. &nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:96px; font-size:11pt">During the year ended June 30, 2008, one customer accounted for 74.4% (2007: two customers accounted for 54.7% and 12.85% respectively) of the Company&#146;s sales. &nbsp;The loss of &nbsp;this customer or the curtailment of purchases by such customer could have a material adverse effect on the Company&#146;s financial condition and results of operations.</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:96px; font-size:11pt">Currency Risk</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:96px; font-size:11pt">The Company holds cash of $414,411 in Canadian dollars exposing it to a foreign currency exchange risk.</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-17.333px; padding-left:72px; font-size:11pt"><U>l)</U></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:72px; text-indent:24px; font-size:11pt"><U>Revenue Recognition</U></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-17.333px; padding-left:96px; font-size:11pt">i)</P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:96px; text-indent:24px; font-size:11pt">Building Supplies</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:120px; font-size:11pt">The Company recognizes revenue in accordance with Securities and Exchange Commission (&#147;SEC&#148;) Staff Accounting Bulletin 104, &#147;Revenue Recognition&#148;, which requires that: (i) persuasive evidence of an arrangement exists, (ii) delivery has occurred, (iii) the sales price is fixed and determinable, and (iv) collectibility is reasonably assured. The Company recognizes revenue when the building supplies have been shipped and the customer has been invoiced. </P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-17.333px; padding-left:144px; text-indent:-48px; font-size:11pt" align=justify>iii)</P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:144px; text-indent:-24px; font-size:11pt" align=justify>License Fees</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:120px; font-size:11pt">License fees revenue is recognized when the licensee records the sale of products from certain fire retardant technology known as IPOSB technology and collection is reasonably assured. There was no license fee revenue during the years ended June 30, 2008 and 2007.</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR>
<BR></P>
<P style="line-height:14pt; margin:0px; font-family:Courier New; font-size:12pt" align=center>39</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<HR style="margin-top:9.6px; margin-bottom:9.6px" noshade size=1.333>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; font-size:11pt; page-break-before:always">International Barrier Technology Inc.</P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; font-size:11pt">Notes to the Consolidated Financial Statements</P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; font-size:11pt">June 30, 2008 and 2007</P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; font-size:11pt">(<U>Stated in US Dollars</U>) &#150; Page 6</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-17.333px; font-size:11pt">Note 2</P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; text-indent:72px; font-size:11pt"><U>Significant Accounting Policies</U> &#150; (cont&#146;d)</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-17.333px; padding-left:72px; font-size:11pt">l)</P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:72px; text-indent:24px; font-size:11pt"><U>Income Taxes</U></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:96px; font-size:11pt">The Company follows the liability method of accounting for income taxes in accordance with SFAS No. 109. &nbsp;Under this method, current income taxes are recognized for the estimated income taxes payable for the current year. &nbsp;Future income tax assets and liabilities are recognized in the current year for temporary differences between the tax and accounting basis of assets and liabilities as well as for the benefit of losses available to be carried forward to future years for tax purposes. &nbsp;Future income tax assets and liabilities are measured using tax rates and laws expected to apply in the years in which those temporary differences are expected to be recovered or settled. &nbsp;The effect of a change in tax rates on future income tax assets and liabilities is recognized in operations in the year of change. &nbsp;Valuation allowances are recorded when it is &#147;more likely-than-not&#148; that a deferred tax asset will n
ot be realized.</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-17.333px; padding-left:72px; font-size:11pt">m)</P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:72px; text-indent:24px; font-size:11pt"><U>Stock-based Compensation</U></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:96px; font-size:11pt"><U>The Company accounts for all stock-based payments and awards under the fair value based method.</U></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:96px; font-size:11pt">Stock-based payments to non-employees are measured at the fair value of the consideration received, or the fair value of the equity instruments issued, or liabilities incurred, whichever is more reliably measurable. The fair value of stock-based payments to non-employees is periodically re-measured until the counterparty performance is complete, and any change therein is recognized over the vesting period of the award and in the same manner as if the Company had paid cash instead of paying with or using equity based instruments. The cost of the stock-based payments to non-employees that are fully vested and non-forfeitable as at the grant date is measured and recognized at that date, unless there is a contractual term for services in which case such compensation would be amortized over the contractual term. </P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:96px; font-size:11pt">The Company accounts for the granting of share purchase options to employees using the fair value method whereby all awards to employees will be recorded at fair value on the date of the grant. &nbsp;The fair value of all share purchase options are expensed over their vesting period with a corresponding increase to additional capital surplus. &nbsp;Upon exercise of share purchase options, the consideration paid by the option holder, together with the amount previously recognized in additional capital surplus, is recorded as an increase to share capital</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:96px; font-size:11pt">The Company uses the Black-Scholes option valuation model to calculate the fair value of share purchase options at the date of the grant. &nbsp;Option pricing models require the input of highly subjective assumptions, including the expected price volatility. &nbsp;Changes in these assumptions can materially affect the fair value estimate.</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-17.333px; padding-left:72px; font-size:11pt">n)</P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:72px; text-indent:24px; font-size:11pt"><U>Comparative Figures</U></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:96px; font-size:11pt">Certain of the comparative figures have been reclassified to conform with the current year&#146;s presentation.</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR>

<HR style="margin-top:9.6px; margin-bottom:9.6px" noshade size=1.333>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; font-size:11pt; page-break-before:always">International Barrier Technology Inc.</P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; font-size:11pt">Notes to the Consolidated Financial Statements</P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; font-size:11pt">June 30, 2008 and 2007</P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; font-size:11pt">(<U>Stated in US Dollars</U>) &#150; Page 7</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-17.333px; font-size:11pt">Note 2</P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; text-indent:72px; font-size:11pt"><U>Significant Accounting Policies</U> &#150; (cont&#146;d)</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-17.333px; padding-left:72px; font-size:11pt">o)</P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:72px; text-indent:24px; font-size:11pt"><U>Recent Accounting Pronouncements</U></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:96px; font-size:11pt">In June 2006, the Financial Accounting Standards Board (&#147;FASB&#148;) issued FASB Interpretation No. 48, &#147;Accounting for Uncertainty in Income Taxes&#148;. &nbsp;The interpretation clarifies the accounting for uncertainty in income taxes recognized in a company&#146;s financial statements in accordance with Statement of Financial Accounting Standards No. 109, &#147;Accounting for Income Taxes&#148;. &nbsp;Specifically, the pronouncement prescribes a recognition threshold and a measurement attribute for the financial statement recognition and measurement of a tax position taken or expected to be taken in a tax return. &nbsp;The interpretation also provides guidance on the related derecognition, classification, interest and penalties, accounting for interim periods, disclosure and transition of uncertain tax position. &nbsp;The interpretation is effective for fiscal years beginning after December 15, 2006. &nbsp;Effective July 
1, 2007, the Company adopted the provisions of FIN 48. Based on the Company&#146;s assessment of FIN 48, as at July 1, 2007, there was no significant impact on the results of operations or financial position and required no adjustment to the opening balance sheet accounts. The Company&#146;s analysis supports the same conclusion, and there is no accrual for uncertain tax positions as of June 30, 2008. As a result, tabular reconciliation of beginning and ending balances would not be meaningful. If interest and penalties were to be assessed, we would charge interest to interest expense, and penalties to other operating expense. It is not anticipated that unrecognized tax benefits would significantly increase or decrease within 12 months of the reporting date. &nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:96px; font-size:11pt">In September 2006, the FASB issued SFAS No. 157, &#147;Fair Value Measurements&#148;. &nbsp;This Statement defines fair value as used in numerous accounting pronouncements, establishes a framework for measuring fair value in generally accepted accounting principles and expands disclosure related to the use of fair value measures in financial statements. &nbsp;SFAS 157 is effective for fiscal years beginning after November 15, 2007. The Company is currently evaluating the timing of adoption and the impact that adoption might have on its financial position or results of operations.</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:96px; font-size:11pt">On February 15, 2007, the FASB issued SFAS No. 159 &#147;The Fair Value Option for Financial Assets and Financial Liabilities&#148;. &nbsp;This Statement establishes presentation and disclosure requirements designed to facilitate comparisons between companies that choose different measurement attributes for similar types of assets and liabilities. &nbsp;SFAS 159 is effective for fiscal years beginning after November 15, 2007. The Company is currently evaluating the impact that the adoption of SFAS No. 159 might have on its financial position or results of operations.</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:96px; font-size:11pt">In December 2007, the FASB issued SFAS 141R &#147;Business Combinations&#148; which is effective for fiscal years beginning after December 15, 2008. SFAS 141R, which will replace FAS 141, is applicable to business combinations consummated after the effective date of December 15, 2008. &nbsp;The Company is currently evaluating the impact that the adoption of SFAS No. 141R might have on its financial position or results of operations.</P>
